<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This letter presents a novel dual-band (HF and UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) tag antenna. Two key challenges are faced: the compact dimension and the impaired bandwidth due to the couplings between two band structures. To enable the implementation of whole design on a credit-card-size single-layer support, a spiral coil along the edges of the card is designed to handle the HF (13.56 MHz) near-field coupling, and the UHF antenna is placed inside the coil instead of outside. Meanwhile, a diagonal symmetric design consisting of two meander lines inside the spiral coil is adopted for UHF band. This structure supports multiple resonance modes around 915 MHz to broaden the working bandwidth under the large inductive circumstance from the HF coil. The proposed antenna is easy for adjustment with ways of handling both coarse tuning and fine-tuning. Its overall dimension is of a credit card size on a single-layer thin substrate. The design methodology and antenna measurement results are both presented and discussed in the letter.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID), as a fast growing technology in recent years, has been applied in many areas, such as logistics, inventory management and bio-engineering, etc. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. To fulfill different kinds of requirements, various communication protocol standards, and operating frequency bands are established. In terms of operating frequency band, HF band is widely applied in short-distance reading applications, such as the campus card system. UHF band is often applied in long-distance reading applications. In addition, the frequency allocations of different countries are quite different. For UHF bands, 866–869 MHz is used in Europe, 902–928 MHz in North and South America, and 950–956 MHz in Japan and some Asian countries <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>.</p><p>For some special cases, like highway tracking and tolls, both short-distance and long-distance reading are needed. Hence, a single RFID card with dual standards is demanded. From an academic point of view, the research on the dual-band antenna with nearly 70 times frequency difference is also an interesting challenge.</p><p>Some research on HF-UHF dual-band antennas has been published in the past few years. Mono feeding port type <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> and dual feeding port type <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> were discussed. For the dual feeding port type, the spiral coil and meander-line dipole are used as the HF antenna and the UHF antenna, respectively. References <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> discussed the case when the UHF antenna is placed outside the HF coil. The mutual interaction issue and decoupling issue between UHF and HF antennas are analyzed. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, studies of integrating the UHF antenna inside the coil are presented. Due to the existence of a large inductive coil, its quality factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.72em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Q</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is very high. For serial circuits, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 5.709em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.108em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.11em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Q</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">Q=\omega_{0}L/R</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the bandwidth is proportional to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-18" role="math" style="width: 2.045em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.805em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.75em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Q</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">1/Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The larger the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-25" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">L</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the narrower the bandwidth. Placing the UHF antenna inside the coil can reduce the whole antenna dimension. However, the narrow band becomes an issue to be solved.</p><p>In this letter, a novel single-layer dual-band RFID tag antenna is presented. Unlike many existing works, it places the UHF antenna inside the HF coil to enable the compact implementation on a credit-card-size substrate. Therefore, the coupling between HF and UHF antennas causes the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-28" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.72em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Q</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the system to be very high at UHF because of the huge parasitic inductance from the HF coil. Hence, the working bandwidth is narrow. To expand the bandwidth, a diagonal symmetric design consisting of two meander lines inside the spiral coil is adopted for the UHF band to support multiple resonance modes around 915 MHz. As a result, both compactness and enough bandwidth are achieved through the proposed design. The design methodology is verified by the measurements including the practical UHF RFID reading range test. It fully demonstrated the feasibility of the proposed idea.</p><p>This letter is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> introduces the antenna's structure and dimensions. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> gives the design methodology and result analysis of HF and UHF parts, respectively. The antenna's operation principle and impedance matching method are discussed.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Structure</h2></div><p>The proposed antenna structure is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. It has two feeding ports connecting HF and UHF RFID chips, respectively. The HF antenna is a spiral coil with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-31" role="math" style="width: 5.048em; Two rectangular slots in two arms are used to fine-tune the impedance. In the simulation and manufacture, we use FR4 (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-264" role="math" style="width: 3.426em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.066em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.01em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-265"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-266" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϵ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-267" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-268" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">4.2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">\epsilon=4.2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-269" role="math" style="width: 5.829em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.17em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-270"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">tan</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-272"></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-273" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">δ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-274" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-275" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.02</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">\tan\delta=0.02</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) substrate with the dimension of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-276" role="math" style="width: 9.072em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 8.171em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1008.17em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-277"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-278" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">85</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-279" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-280" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">54</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-281" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">0.8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-283" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-284"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-287"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-288"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-289" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-291"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-292" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">85\times 54\times 0.8\ {\hbox{mm}}^{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the manufactured antenna. The HF coil is designed for NXP Mifare ASIC that complies with the ISO/IEC 14443 standard. The UHF antenna operates with an Impinj Monza 3 Tag chip that has <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-293" role="math" style="width: 5.769em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.168em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.11em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-294"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-295" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">32</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-296" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-297" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-298" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">216</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-299" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-300" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">32-j216\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> input impedance at 915 MHz and complies with the ISO 18000-6C standard. The typical values of read and write sensitivities for this chip are −15 and −11 dBm, respectively. This design is simulated and optimized in ANSYS HFSS.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Proposed antenna structure.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Antenna Design and Analysis</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. HF Frequency Band</h3><p>In the HF frequency band, the 13.56-MHz antenna operates as the near-field coupling antenna. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-301" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.44em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-303" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">LC</script></tex-math></inline-formula> resonance relationship can be obtained by the microchip's impedance and external spiral coil. The resonance frequency is defined as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-305" role="math" style="width: 6.369em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.709em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.71em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-306"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-307"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-308" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-309"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-310"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-311" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-312" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-315"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="msqrt" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.44em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-318"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-320" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.607em 1001.44em 3.967em -999.997em); top: -4.562em; left: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; font-family: MathJax_Main; top: -4.021em; left: -0.057em;">−<span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; font-family: MathJax_Main; top: -4.021em; left: 0.784em;">−<span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="font-family: MathJax_Main; position: absolute; top: -4.021em; left: 0.363em;">−<span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.066em 1000.84em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.081em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">√</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">\omega_{0}=1/\sqrt{LC}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The microchip's impedance is equivalent to a 17- pF capacitor. Hence, the external coil provides needed inductance. The suitable equivalent inductor of resonance can be achieved by adjusting the line width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-321" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1000.78em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-323"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-324" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-325"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">t_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, line gap distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-328" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-329"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-330" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">D</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, length <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-331" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-332"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-333"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-334" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-335"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-336"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-337" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">L_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-338" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-339"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-340"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-341" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-343"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">W_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the whole coil.</p><p>In practical applications, because the tag will be placed on the reader during the reading process, extra coupling capacitances will be generated by contact. Hence, the resonance frequency without contact should be designed to a little higher frequency than the operating frequency (13.56 MHz). In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_3a">[5]</a>, the authors set the frequency at 16.4 MHz. The band from 14.5 to 18.5 MHz is an acceptable range.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the measured and simulated HF band input impedance. In the simulation, we adjust the coil's parameters to set the input impedance to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-345" role="math" style="width: 6.009em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.408em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.35em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-346"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-347" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2.4</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-348" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-349" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-350" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">544</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-351" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-352" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">2.4+j544\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 13.56 MHz. Combined with the 17-pF equivalent capacitor, the calculated resonance frequency without reader contact is 15.28 MHz. From the measured result, at 13.56 MHz, the impedance is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-353" role="math" style="width: 6.429em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.769em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.71em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-354"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-355" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">5.4</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-356" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-357" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">519.8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-358" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-359" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">5.4+519.8\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This result is very close to the simulated result.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Measured and simulated HF band input impedance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. UHF Frequency Band</h3><p>The UHF antenna design is mainly focused on solving the narrowband issue under large inductance and high quality factor circumstances. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows the input impedance comparison with and without an external coil. It is obvious that the external coil increases the inductor of the UHF antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Input impedance comparison with and without external coil.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The original design intention is to use two dipoles to form two adjacent resonance frequencies to broaden the bandwidth, like the structure proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_3b">[9]</a>. The best expectation is that the two dominant resonance modes could operate independently and have minimum mutual influences. The actual operating condition is more complex. Due to the limitation of compact size, we expect to build up a structure that has multiple potential modes, and then try to excite two of them through some simple adjustments. To add more adjustment capability and ensure multiple modes, this structure is proposed. The diagonal meander lines' dimensions are identical, and each two opposite meander lines parallel along the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-360" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-361"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-362" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis are different in dimensions. This ensures multiple resonance modes.</p><p>According to the antenna design, the equivalent circuit model is given in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. In this figure, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-363" role="math" style="width: 3.607em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.246em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.25em 2.586em -999.997em); Among them, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-425" role="math" style="width: 2.646em; From the structure and its equivalent circuit model, it is easy to excite multiple resonance modes in this antenna. By adjusting four meander lines' dimensions, two adjacent resonance modes around 915 MHz can be easily obtained.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Equivalent circuit of the design at the UHF band.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the simulated and measured reflection coefficient. From the comparison, the simulated and measured data appear to be in a good agreement. Two obvious resonance peaks can be observed. The bandwidth is thereby broadened. In simulation, two resonance frequencies appear at 910 and 920 MHz, respectively. The bandwidth is around 30 MHz. The measured two resonance frequencies are at 911 and 931 MHz, respectively. The bandwidth is around 40 MHz broader than the simulation. It should be noted that all the reflection coefficients in this letter are calculated with respect to the chip impedance. We define the following equation in HFSS to do the calculation: <disp-formula id="" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display" style="text-align: center;"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-435" role="math" style="width: 14.538em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 13.096em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.105em 1012.86em 5.468em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-436"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-437" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Γ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-438" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-439" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">20</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-440" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">∗</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-441" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; <p></p><p>According to the reflection coefficient result, the simulated radiation patterns of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-512" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; The maximum gains are −5.36 and −1.89 dB at 910 and 920 MHz, respectively. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> shows simulated frequency characteristic of the gain. To further analyze the UHF two working modes, the surface current distribution plots under two working modes (910 and 920 MHz) are given in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>.

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Simulated frequency characteristic of the gain.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Surface current distribution plots at (a) 910 and (b) 920 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>To understand the practical performance of the antenna, we measured the UHF antenna's reading range. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a> presents the measurement result. It is conducted with effective radiated power (ERP) 3.28 W and reader sensitivity −74 dBm. The reader is linearly polarized. The maximum reading range is 6.8m and appears at 885 MHz. Another peak range is 4.4 m at 925 MHz. Nonlinear input impedance of the microchip may be the reason causing this resonance frequency shift. Due to the in-band dual resonance feature, there is a less-matching frequency in between two primary matching frequencies. Due to the nonlinearity of the chip impedance and some uncertainty parameters not considered in the simulation, the less-matching frequency point is shifted up a little bit to 920 MHz. It results in the low gain at that point.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Measured reading range.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6335459/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Impedance Matching</h3><p>For single-dipole applications, we have many methods to match the impedance, like T-match, loop coupling, and so on <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_3c">[10]</a>. In this design, we expand the width of the main arm patches to conduct the coarse tuning and use rectangle slots to conduct the fine tuning. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> shows the variation of reflection coefficient changing with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-528" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-530"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-531" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-532"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-533"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-534" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">M_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 6 to 8 mm. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-535" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-536"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-537"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-538" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-539"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-540"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-541" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">M_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s variation changes the coupling capacitors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-542" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.68em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-543"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-544"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-545" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-546"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-547"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-548" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-549" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">C_{\rm C1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-550" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.68em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-553" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-554"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-556" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">8</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">C_{\rm C8}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Hence, the resonance frequencies have corresponding changes. The two slots on the main arm patches are equivalent to adding extra serial impedances to the antenna. The impacts of two slots are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 12</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">13</a>. From these two figures, we find when the slots' dimensions are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-558" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.748em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.69em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-559"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-560" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-561" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-562" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">B</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-563" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-564" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">6</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">A=B=6</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm, the reflection coefficient curve is relatively smoothened and the difference between two peaks is minimum.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6335459/6335459-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Reflection coefficient for various main arm patches width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-565" role="math" style="width: 1.789em; <p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>This letter presents a novel single-layer compact RFID tag antenna, which operates in the HF (13.56 MHz) and UHF (915MHz) bands. It features the credit card compact size, low cost, and easy fabrication. Both operation principles in the HF and UHF band are analyzed and discussed. It solves the narrowband issue under the large inductive circumstance by using two adjacent UHF resonance modes. For the impedance matching, the methods of coarse tuning and fine tuning are also presented. Through practical manufacture and measurement, this antenna shows very good performance.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>

frequency identification (RFID) tag antenna. Two key challenges are faced: the compact dimension and the impaired bandwidth due to the couplings between two band structures. To enable the implementation of whole design on a credit-card-size single-layer support, a spiral coil along the edges of the card is designed to handle the HF (13.56 MHz) near-field coupling, and the UHF antenna is placed inside the coil instead of outside. Meanwhile, a diagonal symmetric design consisting of two meander lines inside the spiral coil is adopted for UHF band. This structure supports multiple resonance modes around 915 MHz to broaden the working bandwidth under the large inductive circumstance from the HF coil. The proposed antenna is easy for adjustment with ways of handling both coarse tuning and fine-tuning. Its overall dimension is of a credit card size on a single-layer thin substrate. The design methodology and antenna measurement results are both presented and discussed in the
